1. (낙관적인) 긍정적인<br/>2. (도움이 되는) 긍정적인<br/>3. (동의・지지하는) 긍정적인
1. (낙관적인) 긍정적인<br/>2. (도움이 되는) 긍정적인<br/>3. (동의・지지하는) 긍정적인
1. 어느 정도, 꽤<br/>2. 아주, 매우<br/>3. (매우 아름답지는 않지만) 매력적인, 예쁜, 귀여운
1. (희귀하고 많은 금전적 가치를 지닌) 귀중한, 값비싼<br/>2. (낭비해서는 안 될) 귀한<br/>3. (개인에게) 소중한
1. 뭐라구요(상대방의 말을 알아듣지 못했을 때 다시 말해 달라는 뜻으로 하는 말)<br/>2. 미안해요(가벼운 실수 등을 했을 때 하는 말)<br/>3. (죄인에 대한) 사면

The subtle and the profound.  Yugen is at the core of the appreciation of beauty and art in Japan. It values the power to evoke, rather that the ability to state directly. The principle of Yugen shows that real beauty exists when, through its suggestiveness, only a few words, or few brush strokes, can suggest what has not been said or shown, and hence awaken many inner thoughts ...

kapish is formally spelled as capisce (pronounced as cah-peesh) which is derived from the italian word capire "to understand" and from latin capere "to grasp or to seize".  it is now used in american slang to say "got it" or "understand."  common alternative spellings you might encounter are capice, capicé, capiche, capeesh, capisch, capishe and coppish.
